2:22:1278:0:14:72:295:700:12:Times:12:Times:?:The Circulation of Ideas in Firms and Markets
2:23:1323:14:14:72:278:686:12:Times:12:Times:?:Thomas F. Hellmann and Enrico C. Perotti
2:24:1363:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 16943
2:25:1391:14:14:72:124:658:12:Times:12:Times:?:April 2011
2:26:1401:14:28:72:230:644:12:Times:12:Times:?:JEL No. D83,L22,L26,M13,O31
2:27:1428:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:A:ABSTRACT
2:28:1436:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:?:Novel early stage ideas face uncertainty on the expertise needed to elaborate them, which creates a
2:29:1535:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:need to circulate them widely to find a match. Yet as information is not excludable, shared ideas may
2:30:1636:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:be stolen, reducing incentives to innovate. Still, in idea-rich environments inventors may share them
2:31:1737:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:without contractual protection. Idea density is enhanced by firms ensuring rewards to inventors, while
2:32:1839:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:their legal boundaries limit idea leakage. As firms limit idea circulation, the innovative environment
2:33:1941:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:involves a symbiotic interaction: firms incubate ideas and allow employees leave if they cannot find
2:34:2041:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:an internal fit; markets allow for wide ideas circulation of ideas until matched and completed; under
2:35:2142:14:42:72:449:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:certain circumstances ideas may be even developed in both firms and markets.
2:36:2218:42:14:72:174:448:12:Times:12:Times:?:Thomas F. Hellmann
2:37:2236:14:14:72:200:434:12:Times:12:Times:?:Sauder School of Business
2:38:2261:14:14:72:222:420:12:Times:12:Times:?:University of British Columbia
2:39:2291:14:14:72:150:406:12:Times:12:Times:?:2053 Main Mall
2:40:2305:14:14:72:194:392:12:Times:12:Times:?:Vancouver, BC V6T 1Z2
2:41:2326:14:14:72:123:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:CANADA
2:42:2332:14:14:72:124:364:12:Times:12:Times:?:and NBER
2:43:2340:14:28:72:193:350:12:Times:12:Times:?:hellmann@sauder.ubc.ca
2:44:2362:28:14:72:153:322:12:Times:12:Times:?:Enrico C. Perotti
2:45:2379:14:14:72:183:308:12:Times:12:Times:?:Department of Finance
2:46:2400:14:14:72:195:294:12:Times:12:Times:?:University of Amsterdam
2:47:2423:14:14:72:145:280:12:Times:12:Times:?:Roeterstraat 11
2:48:2438:14:14:72:180:266:12:Times:12:Times:?:1018  WB Amsterdam

3:51:2485:0:30:89:225:707:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:1  Introduction
3:52:2500:30:18:89:520:677:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The role of innovation in economic growth is well recognized (Romer, 1990), yet the
3:53:2583:18:18:89:520:659:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:process of generating innovative ideas is still a novelfield. The literature has focused
3:54:2671:18:18:89:520:641:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:on intellectual property rights as incentive for invention (Nordhaus, 1969, Gallini and
3:55:2758:18:18:89:520:623:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Scotchmer, 2001). We focus here on an earlier stage in the innovation process, when
3:56:2841:18:18:89:520:605:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:novel but incomplete ideas are too vague to be granted patent rights, since they are
3:57:2925:18:18:89:520:587:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:still half-baked and in need of further elaboration. While the development of standard
3:58:3011:18:18:89:520:569:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideas can be planned, for truly novel concepts the next step for their development is
3:59:3096:18:18:89:521:551:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:unclear, and the missing expertise cannot be identified ex ante. So new ideas need
3:60:3178:18:18:89:521:533:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to circulate widely tofind the right match. This exposes inventors to the risk of idea
3:61:3264:18:18:89:284:515:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:theft as information is not excludable.
3:62:3303:18:17:107:521:497:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:To understand this trade-off, we study an environment when all agents choose
3:63:3379:17:18:89:520:480:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:whether to produce ideas or to seek to elaborate ideas of others. Our fundamental
3:64:3460:18:18:89:520:462:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:assumptions are that early stage ideas are half-baked and valueless until elaborated
3:65:3544:18:18:89:521:444:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:further by another individual with the right complementary expertise (which we term
3:66:3627:18:18:89:524:426:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:acomplementor). Whenanagentwithanideaismatchedwithacomplementor,it
3:67:3693:18:18:89:521:408:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is optimal for them to cooperate to develop the concept.1The problem of idea theft
3:68:3775:18:18:89:521:390:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:arises when the matched individual lacks the complementaryfit, but acquires the
3:69:3854:18:18:89:113:372:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea.
3:70:3859:18:18:107:521:354:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The common assumption in the literature is that agents cannot commit not to
3:71:3934:18:18:89:520:336:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:steal an idea before hearing it.  According to Arrow (1962), a listener to an idea
3:72:4016:18:18:89:520:318:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:would not know how to price it, yet afterwards it is no longer optimal to pay the
3:73:4097:18:18:89:520:300:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:disclosing party. Indeed, agents frequently involved in assessing new ideas, such as
3:74:4181:18:18:89:520:282:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:venture capitalists, academic researchers and Hollywood producers, routinely refuse
3:75:4264:18:18:89:307:264:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to sign non-disclosure agreements (NDAs).
3:76:4305:18:17:107:521:246:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We seek to answer two basic questions.  Why, if asking for an NDA is always
3:77:4380:17:18:89:521:229:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:beneficial for the issuer, would the other party not agree to sign it? Prior literature
3:78:4467:18:18:89:520:211:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:points to contractual imperfections and the possibility of extortion (Anton and Yao,
3:79:4551:18:18:89:521:193:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2002, 2003, 2004).2Second, if indeed most ideas are shared without contractual
3:80:4629:18:18:89:520:175:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:protection, how can inventors protect their claim? Previous work has analyzed the
3:81:4710:18:16:103:520:157:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:1Cooperation is possible as ideas are in principle contractible: if they are shared verbally, they
3:82:4808:16:8:89:205:141:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:may also be written down.
3:83:4833:8:15:103:520:133:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2NDAs are sometimes employed at late stages of idea elaboration, to formalize commitments to
3:84:4925:15:0:89:306:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:awelldefined project (Bagley and Dauchy, 2008).
4:85:4973:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:problem of sharing a single idea between two agents (Anton and Yao 1994, 2004),
4:86:5052:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:while we examine the creation and circulation of many ideas among a large set of
4:87:5132:18:18:89:124:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents.
4:88:5139:18:18:107:526:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Inthemodel,ateachdateagentschoosewhethertoinvent,ortobematched
4:89:5201:18:18:89:524:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with agents who may either have ideas or be free-riding as well. If a goodfitisfound
4:90:5285:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for an idea, both parties have incentives to cooperate. However, if the idea is shared
4:91:5371:18:18:89:524:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with someone unable to elaborate it, therecanbenogainfromcooperating.Soinan
4:92:5446:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:open market exchange, ideas circulate through a sequence of agents, not necessarily
4:93:5529:18:18:89:520:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:their inventors, until matched to a complementor. From an ex-post perspective, a free
4:94:5614:18:18:89:520:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:circulation of ideas is most efficient in ensuring their elaboration. However, frequent
4:95:5701:18:18:89:488:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea stealing may deny the inventor a sufficient reward for the initial concept.
4:96:5781:18:18:107:520:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Wefirst derive the conditions under which idea protection fails endogenously.
4:97:5858:18:18:89:520:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Agents have limited memory so they can recall at most one idea.  We show that
4:98:5935:18:18:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:there always exists an equilibrium where no one signs NDAs, even for an arbitrarily
4:99:6018:18:17:89:520:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:small drafting cost. In addition, when ideas are sufficiently frequent, there may be no
4:100:6105:17:18:89:521:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibria where all agents sign NDAs.3In general, ideas will circulate unprotected
4:101:6188:18:18:89:411:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:when the threat not to disclose without a NDA is not credible.
4:102:6250:18:18:107:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Next we seek to understand what context creates high idea density to compensate
4:103:6329:18:18:89:521:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:forideastealing. Wearguethatnexttoindependentagents,firms are a source of
4:104:6402:18:18:89:521:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideas because they can create an internal environment where ideas can be shared and
4:105:6485:18:18:89:520:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea generation can be rewarded. We argue that such an environment requires that
4:106:6565:18:18:89:521:330:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms to develop a local reputation for transparency among its employees. In addition,
4:107:6651:18:18:89:521:312:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms use their legal boundary to control the leaking of internal idea, ensuring a safe
4:108:6738:18:18:89:206:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:internal idea exchange.
4:109:6761:18:18:107:521:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Yetsomeideaswillnotberesolvedwithinfirms when no matching skill is found.
4:110:6834:18:18:89:521:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Open knowledge strategies allow unresolved ideas to leave thefirm to spawn new
4:111:6912:18:18:89:521:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ventures. So markets benefits from idea incubators such asfirms (or academic insti-
4:112:6995:18:17:89:520:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tutions) to increase the rate of idea generation. As a conclusion, coexistence of open
4:113:7081:17:18:89:521:205:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms and markets produces an optimal environment for idea generation and their
4:114:7160:18:18:89:254:187:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:completion by wider circulation.
4:115:7192:18:18:107:521:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In this approach,firms can emerge as a solution to a market failure where agents
4:116:7272:18:16:103:521:151:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:3This reflects a similar paradox as in Grossman and Stiglitz (1983), who show thatfinancial
4:117:7363:16:12:89:520:135:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:prices cannot be fully informative as there would be no gain to collect information. In our context,
4:118:7463:12:0:89:521:123:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:if there is no risk of idea theft there are no opportunists, so at the margin the NDAs are superfluous.
5:119:7567:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:who accept employment are bound by trade secret law, which can be thought of
5:120:7643:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as a collective non-disclosure agreement.  In exchange, thefirm has to commit to
5:121:7723:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:reward creative employees, a commitment which we argue need to be backed by
5:122:7798:18:18:89:521:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:reputation. We assume that afirm owner can make a costly investment in building
5:123:7877:18:18:89:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a local reputation by creating visibility of her actions among thefirm’s employees
5:124:7959:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(Kreps, 1986). The threat of loss of corporate reputation for fair dealing ensures that
5:125:8046:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:employees agree to contractually commit to sharing and not stealing ideas inside the
5:126:8130:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firm, even though they may refuse to sign an equivalent contract with an individual
5:127:8213:18:18:89:520:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agent who has more limited visibility and thus a limited punishment in case of breach.
5:128:8299:18:18:89:521:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:As the employment contract implies respect forfirm trade secrets, thefirm can provide
5:129:8384:18:18:89:391:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a safe idea exchange, and a safer return to idea generators.
5:130:8444:18:18:107:521:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Firms incur costs for reputation creation and monitoring theflow of ideas, so
5:131:8521:18:18:89:521:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the density offirms depends on their return relative to independent activity. But
5:132:8602:18:18:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the fundamental cost of afirm here is that it contains idea circulation withinfirm
5:133:8684:18:17:89:520:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:boundaries, thus limiting the set of possible matching expertise. This leads to our
5:134:8767:17:18:89:521:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:second main result: just as market failure creates a need for idea-incubatingfirms,
5:135:8850:18:18:89:521:420:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firm failure to develop some internal projects creates a role for markets to complete
5:136:8935:18:18:89:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:those ideas, increasing the density offirms in the market.  This requiresfirms to
5:137:9016:18:18:89:520:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:pursue an open knowledge approach, allowing employees to spin-offtheir ideas that
5:138:9097:18:18:89:520:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:could not be used internally (Lewis and Yao, 2003; Sevilir, 2009).  Thus, in our
5:139:9177:18:18:89:521:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:approachfirms and markets complement one another, each compensating for some
5:140:9253:18:18:89:521:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inefficiency of the other. Firms incubate ideas, while markets increase their chances
5:141:9338:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of elaboration. This complementarity suggests a natural symbiosis of openfirms and
5:142:9420:18:48:89:478:294:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:markets, as it is the case in innovative environments such as Silicon Valley.4
5:143:9498:48:47:107:394:246:301:g_d0_f2:301:g_d0_f2:A:Relationship to the theoretical literature
5:144:9540:47:18:107:521:199:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Following Schumpeter (1926, 1942), this paper treats a new idea as a novel com-
5:145:9619:18:18:89:520:181:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:bination of existing factors (see also Biais and Perotti, 2008, and Weitzman, 1998).
5:146:9703:18:18:89:521:163:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In the case of a truly novel idea, unlike conventional team production, the process of
5:147:9789:18:18:89:520:145:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:discovery by matching skills cannot be planned. As a result, a broad circulation of
5:148:9872:18:16:103:521:127:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:4Note that byfirms we mean large multi-projectfirms, rather than entrepreneurial single-project
5:149:9967:16:0:89:276:111:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:start-ups which we associate with markets.
6:150:10010:0:18:89:524:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideasiscriticalforinnovation,asitallowsmaximumchanceofelaboration.Saxenian
6:151:10084:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(1994) emphasizes “cross-pollination” and open networking as a main cause of Silicon
6:152:10168:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Valley’s innovative success. We can rationalize such an environment thanks to the
6:153:10249:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:explicit dynamic game where idea density sustains their free circulation. Haessler et
6:154:10334:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:al. (2009) show that idea sharing may occur in a dynamic model with repeated inter-
6:155:10417:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:action, and provide some supporting evidence. For a fascinating review of historical
6:156:10501:18:18:89:431:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:periods of high idea density and free circulation, see Meyer (2003).
6:157:10569:18:18:107:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The literature on innovation has long recognized the non-excludability of informa-
6:158:10651:18:18:89:520:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tion as a key obstacle for innovation. Aghion and Tirole (1994) studied the optimal
6:159:10734:18:18:89:520:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:allocation of control over innovative ideas. Anton and Yao (1994) show that inventors
6:160:10819:18:18:89:520:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:can ex-post secure some value by threatening to transmit the idea more broadly, cre-
6:161:10903:18:18:89:520:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ating more competitors. Anton and Yao (2002, 2004) show how partial or sequential
6:162:10984:18:18:89:521:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:disclosure of ideas helps inventors secure a larger payoff(see also Bhattacharya and
6:163:11068:18:18:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Guriev, 2006, and Cestone and White, 2003)). The basic mechanism is the threat
6:164:11146:18:17:89:520:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to disseminate an idea if stolen. Some papers considers instead limiting the circula-
6:165:11231:17:18:89:520:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tion of ideas. Baccara and Razin (2006, 2008) examine whether inventors may buy
6:166:11310:18:18:89:521:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:out all idea holders, or allow some leakage. Rajan and Zingales (2001) examine how
6:167:11392:18:18:89:520:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a hierarchy may prevent idea-stealing by granting access to its technology only to
6:168:11474:18:18:89:520:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:dedicated employees. Ueda (2004) and Chemmanur and Chen (2006) examines the
6:169:11549:18:18:89:521:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:trade-offof talking to uninformed investors versus venture capitalists who may steal
6:170:11633:18:18:89:520:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the idea. Silveira and Wright (2007) examine a matching model where non-rival ideas
6:171:11716:18:18:89:521:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:can be traded. Idea diffusion models where the number of agents with the same idea
6:172:11798:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:increases over time are quite complex, so our focus is on the simpler case of (ex post
6:173:11884:18:18:89:310:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:efficient) idea circulation without diffusion.
6:174:11930:18:18:107:521:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Biais and Perotti (2008) show that an unpatentable idea may be safely shared with
6:175:12011:18:18:89:520:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents known to be highly complementary experts, and implemented by a contingent
6:176:12091:18:18:89:521:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:partnership.  This paper pursues the effect of complementarity one step further -
6:177:12172:18:18:89:520:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:or rather earlier - by allowing the complementary agent not just to screen, but to
6:178:12254:18:18:89:520:204:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:elaborate the idea. In a related approach, Stein (2008) studies the complementar-
6:179:12335:18:17:89:520:186:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ity of information shared sequentially in the elaboration of a project. Bolton and
6:180:12417:17:18:89:520:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Dewatripont (1994), and Novaes and Zingales (2004) examine idea generation and
6:181:12495:18:18:89:521:151:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:communication withinfirms. Johnson (2002) and Lerner and Tirole (2002) examine
6:182:12573:18:18:89:303:133:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea exchanges in an open-source context.
6:183:12614:18:0:107:521:115:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In our model,firms emerge to compensate for opportunism in market interaction,
7:184:12693:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as in Coase (1937). Holmström and Roberts (1998) suggest that ideas, and the people
7:185:12776:18:18:89:521:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:who generate them, belong at the core of any theory of thefirm. An employee’s idea
7:186:12858:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is an intangible real asset in principle owned by thefirm, but which cannot be claimed
7:187:12944:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:unless the employee reports it. Loss offirm reputation to reward invention (Kreps,
7:188:13026:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:1986) is costlier than the breach of an individual promise observed by few other
7:189:13106:18:18:89:124:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents.
7:190:13113:18:18:107:521:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In section 2 we develop the basic model, focusing on idea sharing in markets and
7:191:13193:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the use of precontracting with NDAs. Section 3 studies idea circulation withinfirms
7:192:13276:18:18:89:521:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and acrossfirm boundaries, wherefirms and markets coexist.  Section 4 presents
7:193:13354:18:18:89:521:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:simple extensions and discusses the empirical evidence, in particular on openfirm en-
7:194:13439:18:45:89:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:vironments andfirm spawning. We conclude with some thoughts for further research.
7:195:13520:45:34:89:463:482:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:2  Idea circulation in a pure market setting
7:196:13564:34:26:89:254:448:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.1  Basic assumptions
7:197:13586:26:18:89:521:422:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Wefirst examine the interaction among market agents in an environment without
7:198:13663:18:18:89:521:404:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:anyfirms. The base model has an infinite number of periods, with a discount factor
7:199:13745:18:17:89:353:386:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ofδ. All agents are risk-neutral and infinitely-lived.
7:200:13799:17:18:107:521:369:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We assume that ideas are too preliminary to be patentable. However, we assume
7:201:13876:18:18:89:520:351:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that it is possible to write down ideas, and therefore to contract on ideas.  Non
7:202:13957:18:18:89:520:333:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Disclosure Agreements (NDAs henceforth) can be used to contractually protect idea.
7:203:14039:18:18:89:520:315:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Whether agents choose to contract or not is endogenous. In sections 2.1 - 2.6 we
7:204:14119:18:18:89:520:297:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:simplify the exposition by assuming that agents do not use any NDAs; Section 2.7
7:205:14199:18:18:89:520:279:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:examines the model with NDAs; Section 2.8 derives the conditions under which agent
7:206:14281:18:18:89:204:261:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:do or don’t use NDAs.
7:207:14302:18:18:107:521:243:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:At the beginning of each period, agents decide whether to generate an idea, or
7:208:14380:18:18:89:521:225:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:interact with others to elaborate ideas (later we let agents also startfirms). Each
7:209:14463:18:18:89:521:207:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:activity lasts one period. Generating an idea requires a private costψ, and we denote
7:210:14548:18:18:89:520:189:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea generators byG. For simplicity we assume that each agent always succeeds to
7:211:14628:18:18:89:520:171:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generating an idea, which he will seek to complete with someone else the following
7:212:14710:18:18:89:521:153:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:period.5All active agents (i.e., not busy generating ideas) are matched at random.
7:213:14792:18:16:103:521:135:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:5An earlier version of the paper allowed for a more general specification where the probability
7:214:14887:16:12:89:521:119:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:of success was a parameterγ∈(0,1]. The comparative statics ofγwere straightforward, so we
7:215:14976:12:0:89:247:107:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:simplifythemodelbysettingγ=1.
8:216:15006:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We denoted byI“idea-bearing” agents have ideas to elaborate (whether their own
8:217:15084:18:18:89:521:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:creation or stolen in previous periods). Agents without any idea, denoted byO(or
8:218:15164:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:“opportunists”), seek a match to elaborate others’ ideas without contributing an idea
8:219:15249:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:themselves. Ideas can be carried across periods, although due to limited memory
8:220:15328:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:each agent can remember one idea at most. Whether an active agent carries a valid
8:221:15409:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea can only be ascertained when the agents interact after being matched. Matched
8:222:15491:18:18:89:521:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents cannot observe each other’s prior history. Since there is an infinite number of
8:223:15577:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents active in the market, the chance that two agents are matched repeatedly is
8:224:15658:18:18:89:140:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:negligible.
8:225:15669:18:18:107:521:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Successful elaboration of an idea requires an idea-specificfit between individual
8:226:15750:18:18:89:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:skills, which cannot be identified ex-ante. Thus tofind out whether an ideafits the
8:227:15833:18:18:89:521:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:skills of two agents, it needs to be shared.6Denote the probability of an idea-specific
8:228:15920:18:18:89:521:491:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:fitbyφ, the chance that the idea-bearerfinds a “complementor” by a random match.
8:229:16000:18:17:89:521:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:With probabilityφthere is nofit, and the two agents are “substitutes”.7Two matched
8:230:16082:17:18:89:521:456:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents share their ideas, so every match shares zero, one or two ideas. When an idea
8:231:16166:18:18:89:521:438:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:finds the matched skill to complete it, it can get implemented by a cooperative effort,
8:232:16253:18:18:89:220:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generating a net payoffz.
8:233:16278:18:18:107:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:If two well-matched agents fail to cooperate and seek to implement the idea with
8:234:16358:18:18:89:520:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:someone else in a later period, competition is such that the sum of their expected
8:235:16440:18:18:89:526:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:individual returnsz0is less than the cooperative return, i.e.,z>2z0.Moreover,the
8:236:16520:18:18:89:521:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:delay reduces the discounted value of the payoff. This ensures that once two agents
8:237:16603:18:18:89:521:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:have an idea thatfits, cooperation is the efficient strategy. If instead there is nofit,
8:238:16691:18:18:89:524:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:theagentsoptimallyagreeonwhoshouldcontinuetopursuetheideafurthertoavoid
8:239:16762:18:18:89:157:294:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:competition.8
8:240:16775:18:18:107:521:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Each period of interaction has three stages. First, the two agents share their own
8:241:16857:18:18:89:521:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideas tofind out whether there is afit. If there is afit, the two agents negotiate
8:242:16939:18:17:89:521:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the sharing of profit, sign an agreement and implement the developed project. Two
8:243:17020:17:18:89:360:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents can implement two projects at the same time.
8:244:17071:18:18:107:521:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In any given period there are three types of agents: Agents working on their own,
8:245:17152:18:16:103:520:187:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:6In Hellmann and Perotti (2005), we consider the case where agents know but can hide their type.
8:246:17248:16:12:89:520:171:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:In this case, substitutes may misrepresent their types, discouraging idea-bearers from pursuing their
8:247:17349:12:9:89:224:159:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:idea, and then secretly steal it.
8:248:17382:9:12:103:520:150:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:7Throughout the paper a bar above a probability denotes its complement, so thatφ≡1−φ..
8:249:17468:12:15:103:521:138:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:8Since the idea is contractible, a feasible implementation of the ex post efficient noncompetitive
8:250:17566:15:0:89:520:123:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:arrangement is that the two agents contract that the winner of a coin toss is the owner of the idea.
9:251:17667:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:termed “generators”, attempt to generate new ideas and are not matched for the
9:252:17745:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:period. Matched agents may be either “idea-bearers” or “opportunists” with no own
9:253:17826:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea to share. We denote the relative fraction of these three types bynG,nIandnO,
9:254:17907:18:18:89:217:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:wherenG+nI+nO=1.
9:255:17923:18:18:107:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:A critical variable which the model endogenizes is the density of ideas in circula-
9:256:18006:18:33:89:441:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tion, measured by the fractionθof matched agents carrying an idea:
9:257:18072:33:0:273:291:584:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f10:A:θ=
9:258:18074:0:16:310:321:592:145:g_d0_f5:65:g_d0_f11:?:nI
9:259:18076:16:26:296:335:576:145:g_d0_f5:65:g_d0_f11:A:nI+nO
9:260:18081:26:18:89:521:550:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:This fractionθof agents who carry ideas reflect individual choices to either spend
9:261:18163:18:18:89:520:532:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:time developing an idea or to act opportunistically.  The model endogenizes this
9:262:18243:18:18:89:521:514:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:natural metric for the degree of innovation in the economy under different forms of
9:263:18326:18:39:89:359:496:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea exchange. We start with pure market exchange.
9:264:18376:39:25:89:203:457:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.2  Bargaining
9:265:18391:25:18:89:521:432:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We assume that all bargaining follows the Nash solution.9As we will see below,
9:266:18469:18:18:89:520:414:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:most bargaining situations in this model are perfectly symmetric, so other bargaining
9:267:18554:18:18:89:521:396:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:solutions, such as Rubinstein’s (1982) alternating offer game, yield the same results.
9:268:18640:18:18:89:520:378:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Wefirst examine the bargaining game in the absence of any NDAs. Section 2.7 will
9:269:18720:18:18:89:249:360:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:address bargaining with NDAs.
9:270:18749:18:18:107:521:342:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The bargaining situation naturally differs according to how many ideas are present,
9:271:18832:18:18:89:521:324:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and how many ideasfit. Considerfirst the case where there is only one idea, and
9:272:18911:18:18:89:521:306:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:it doesn’tfit - this happens with2θθφ. Because ideas can be stolen, both parties
9:273:18991:18:18:89:520:288:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:have the same outside option, irrespective of which partner had idea. However, since
9:274:19075:18:18:89:521:270:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:z>2z0, it is optimal to avoid competition. The two agents agree that only one of
9:275:19155:18:19:89:521:252:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:them should take the idea into the next period. It is therefore optimal toflip an even
9:276:19241:19:0:89:433:233:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:coin, i.e., to let either agent take the idea further with probability
9:277:19311:0:16:439:445:241:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:1
9:278:19312:16:0:439:445:225:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:2
9:279:19313:0:18:446:528:233:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:?:.Ideastealing
9:280:19326:18:18:89:520:215:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:thus occurs in equilibrium, and it is overt, in the sense that both parties are fully
9:281:19411:18:15:89:155:197:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:aware of it.10
9:282:19425:15:16:103:520:182:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:9Binmore, Rubinstein and Wolinsky (1986) provide a foundation for the use of the Nash bargain-
9:283:19519:16:12:89:521:166:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:ing solution, as the outcome of an alternating offer bargaining game with an infinitesimal probability
9:284:19621:12:8:89:215:154:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:that a player exits the game.
9:285:19650:8:16:99:521:146:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:10We may ask how to enforce this efficient continuation. The two agents can write a contract
9:286:19742:16:12:89:520:130:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:that guarantees one of them the right to continue. Such a contract can be thought of as an ex-post
9:287:19840:12:11:89:521:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:nondisclosure agreement. This is fundamentally different from an ex-ante nondisclosure agreement,
9:288:19937:11:0:89:521:107:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:since at the ex-post stage, both agents know the idea and want to ensure that only one of the carries
10:289:20039:0:18:107:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Consider next the case where there is only one idea, and itfits - this happens with
10:290:20122:18:18:89:521:689:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f2:B:2θθφ.Sincez>2z0,itisalwaysefficient to implement the project, generating a joint
10:291:20202:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:value ofz. The outside options of both agents are again symmetric, because of idea
10:292:20284:18:19:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:stealing. That is, in case of disagreement the situation is similar to the above, i.e.,
10:293:20371:19:0:89:313:634:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:each partner takes the idea with probability
10:294:20415:0:17:319:325:642:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:1
10:295:20416:17:0:319:325:625:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:2
10:296:20417:0:23:326:521:634:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:. The equilibrium bargaining outcome
10:297:20453:23:0:89:338:611:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is therefore an equal split, where each agent gets
10:298:20503:0:16:344:349:619:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f5:C:z

13:474:27043:0:33:392:396:488:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:A:.
13:475:27044:33:18:107:521:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 1 states that it is socially optimal not to have any opportunists. The
13:476:27126:18:18:89:520:437:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:intuition is simple. When an idea-bearer is matched with an opportunist, he gets the
13:477:27210:18:18:89:520:419:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:same expected feedback, but as the opportunist has no valid idea, he cannot provide
13:478:27293:18:18:89:521:401:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:any useful feedback. It is therefore always more efficient to match an idea-bearer with
13:479:27380:18:38:89:459:383:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:another idea-bearer. All agents without ideas should generate new ones.
13:480:27451:38:26:89:476:345:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.6  Equilibrium rewards to invention and elaboration
13:481:27504:26:18:89:521:319:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Generators need to achieve a non-negative utility by creating an idea, i.e.,UG≥0.
13:482:27585:18:18:89:521:301:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Any agent without an idea will choose between generating an idea versus listening
13:483:27666:18:18:89:521:283:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to others’, which impliesUG(θ)=UO(θ).  This indifference condition drives the
13:484:27743:18:18:89:521:265:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:density of ideas, as measured byθ. We denote variables associated with the market
13:485:27824:18:27:89:264:247:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium by the superscriptM.
13:486:27856:27:21:89:298:220:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f19:C:Proposition 2(Market equilibrium)

13:492:27971:18:18:89:385:162:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:(i) Ifψ≥ψM, then no ideas are generated in the market.

14:509:28160:51:18:89:521:621:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:(iii) In comparison to the socially efficient outcome, the market equilibrium has a
14:510:28243:18:18:89:521:603:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:smaller feasible range (i.e.,ψM<ψS), fewer generators (nMG<nSG), fewer idea-
14:511:28319:18:17:89:521:585:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:bearers (nMI<nSI), more opportunists (nMO>nSO=0), a lower utility for generators
14:512:28399:17:28:89:390:568:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:(UG<USG), and a lower utility for idea-bearers (UI<USI).
14:513:28455:28:18:107:521:540:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 2 shows how in a pure market setting, idea generation occurs for lower
14:514:28537:18:18:89:521:522:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generation costs than the socially optimalψS,soforanyψ∈[ψM,ψS), idea generation
14:515:28616:18:18:89:520:504:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:would be socially desirable, yet it cannot be achieved in a market exchange. Even
14:516:28697:18:18:89:520:486:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:if idea generation is feasible in the market, its equilibrium return is inefficient since
14:517:28786:18:18:89:520:468:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents can participate in elaborating ideas without contributing any. The market
14:518:28866:18:18:89:528:450:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium always contains less idea-bearers than optimal, i.e.,θ<1.Toseethat
14:519:28944:18:18:89:520:432:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the utility of generating ideas is lower than the socially desirable level we then note
14:520:29031:18:18:89:521:414:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:from Propositions 1 and 2 that∆<∆S, implying that the premium for having an
14:521:29106:18:18:89:398:396:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea in the market is too low relative to the social optimum.
14:522:29167:18:46:107:305:378:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The comparative statics are as follows.
14:523:29206:46:18:107:521:332:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f1:A:Corollary to Proposition 2: Comparative statics of market equilibrium
14:524:29275:18:18:107:349:314:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Consider the market equilibrium withψ<ψM.
14:525:29316:18:18:89:521:296:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(i) The equilibrium number of generators (nMG)isincreasinginzandφ, and decreasing
14:526:29397:18:18:89:114:278:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inψ.
14:527:29401:18:18:89:527:260:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(ii) The equilibrium number of opportunists (nMO)isdecreasinginzandφ,and
14:528:29473:18:18:89:169:242:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:increasing inψ.
14:529:29488:18:18:89:521:224:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(iii) The equilibrium number of idea-bearers (nMI)isincreasinginz, and decreasing
14:530:29569:18:18:89:521:206:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inψ.Itisalsoincreasinginφfor larger values ofψ, but decreasing inφfor smaller
14:531:29646:18:17:89:149:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:values ofψ.
14:532:29657:17:47:89:514:171:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(iv) The utilitiesUG,UIandUOare all increasing inzandφ, and decreasing inψ.
14:533:29732:47:18:107:521:124:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:These results are quite intuitive, as the number of opportunists responds to eco-
14:534:29813:18:0:89:520:106:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:nomic variables in exactly the opposite way as the number of generators. The more
15:535:29896:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:attractive it is to generate ideas, the fewer agents seek to only listen to other agents’
15:536:29985:18:18:89:521:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideas. The more subtle result concernsφ, the probability offit. A higher likelihood
15:537:30068:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:offit encourages ideas generation, but also increases the expected speed at which
15:538:30149:18:18:89:521:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideas get implemented. Higher values ofφare thus associated with more ‘new’ but
15:539:30228:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:fewer ‘old’ ideas. The net effect can go either way. The appendix shows that there
15:540:30310:18:18:89:521:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exists a critical valueψφ∈(0,ψM)such that the ‘new’ idea effect dominates the
15:541:30387:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:‘old’ idea effect if and only ifψ>ψφ. Finally, note that in equilibrium the utility
15:542:30470:18:18:89:520:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of opportunists - unlike the number of opportunists - remains equal to the utility of
15:543:30555:18:39:89:145:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generators.
15:544:30566:39:25:89:413:524:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.7  Equilibrium with perfect idea protection
15:545:30611:25:18:89:520:499:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The analysis so far rules out the protection of ideas via NDAs. We now examine
15:546:30689:18:18:89:520:481:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:NDAs in two steps. This subsection assumes that it is feasible to protect an idea by
15:547:30773:18:18:89:520:463:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inducing a counterpart to sign an NDA. We thus derive the market equilibrium with
15:548:30854:18:18:89:520:445:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:NDAs. In section 2.8 we then derive under what circumstances NDAs are actually
15:549:30932:18:18:89:209:427:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:adopted in equilibrium.
15:550:30955:18:18:107:521:409:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:An agent who seeks to protect his idea is termed the “issuer” of the NDA, and the
15:551:31036:18:18:89:520:391:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agent who agrees not to steal the idea is the “signee” of the NDA. We assume that
15:552:31117:18:18:89:520:373:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:matched partners either agree to sign mutual NDAs, so that each agent becomes both
15:553:31199:18:18:89:520:355:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an issuer and a signee, or neither does. If an agent turns out to be an opportunist,
15:554:31283:18:18:89:520:337:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:issuing a NDA is useless but is harmless.  Each agent incurs an arbitrarily small
15:555:31364:18:18:89:521:319:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:transaction costc>0every time he agrees to a mutual NDA. Our analysis does not
15:556:31442:18:18:89:513:301:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:rely on large transactionc, whose role is merely to break an indifference condition.
15:557:31526:18:18:107:521:283:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:If NDAs are signed by all, any inventor keeps his idea until implementation. This
15:558:31607:18:18:89:521:265:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:increases his bargaining power in case of afit. Interestingly, the NDA protects the
15:559:31690:18:17:89:520:247:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:inventor’s claim on the idea, but does not grant him the full return to his idea. The
15:560:31775:17:18:89:520:230:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:complementor has some bargaining power, since his skills are required for implemen-
15:561:31858:18:18:89:520:212:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tation and seeking another one would imply a delay and thus a lower discounted
15:562:31936:18:18:89:118:194:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:value.
15:563:31942:18:18:107:521:176:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Let the superscriptNdenote variables associated with the NDA equilibrium. To
15:564:32018:18:18:89:526:158:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:derive the Nash bargaining solution, letsbe the profitshareoftheidea-bearer.
15:565:32094:18:18:89:521:140:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ConsiderthecasewhereAhas an idea thatfits, andBis an opportunist without

16:567:32252:0:18:89:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cooperation isz, with continuation utilitiesδUNOforAandB.A’s outside option is to
16:568:32333:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:take the idea back into the market next period, which gives him a continuation value
16:569:32417:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:δUNI.Bcannot steal the idea, so his outside option isδUNO. The Nash bargaining
16:570:32495:18:36:89:359:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:solution therefore implies thatA’s utility is given by

16:610:33491:18:17:89:521:209:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:fraction of idea-bearers is given byθ=1. The equilibrium is the same as the socially
16:611:33575:17:16:99:520:192:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:13Could an idea-bearer do even better by asking the counterpart to accept a contract even more
16:612:33669:16:12:89:521:176:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:onerous than an NDA, such as a contract that gives the idea bearer all of the surplus (i.e.,s=1)?
16:613:33766:12:12:89:521:164:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:The problem is that such contracts would not be renegotiation-proof. Before agreeing to cooperate,
16:614:33864:12:12:89:521:152:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:the complementor can always renegotiate terms. The renegotiation bargaining game is identical to
16:615:33960:12:12:89:520:140:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:the one described above - it is easy to see that the joint value and the outside options are identical
16:616:34062:12:12:89:520:128:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:- implying that the outcome after renegotiation is the same as above. Hence there is no loss of
16:617:34157:12:0:89:308:116:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:generality limiting our analysis to NDA contracts.
17:618:34209:0:20:89:521:707:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:efficient equilibrium, except for the transaction costs, so that we replace∆Swith
17:619:34290:20:0:89:118:687:145:g_d0_f17:145:g_d0_f10:C:∆Sc=
17:620:34294:0:16:122:177:695:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f5:C:φz+ψ−c
17:621:34300:16:0:133:167:679:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f5:C:1+δφ
17:622:34304:0:21:178:182:687:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:A:.
17:623:34305:21:18:89:521:666:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:(iv) The range of the NDA equilibrium lies in between the simple market equilibrium
17:624:34388:18:17:89:389:648:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:and the socially efficient equilibrium, i.e.,ψM<ψN<ψS.
17:625:34442:17:18:89:521:631:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:(v) ForψO<ψ≤ψN, the are more generators than in the market equilibrium, but
17:626:34517:18:18:89:521:613:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:fewer than in the socially efficient equilibrium (nG<nNG<nSG). Same for idea-bearers
17:627:34601:18:18:89:521:595:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:(nMI<nNI<nSI). There are fewer opportunists than in the market equilibrium, but
17:628:34680:18:18:89:520:577:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:more than in the socially efficient equilibrium (nMO>nNO>nSO=0). The utilities
17:629:34758:18:18:89:521:559:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:are higher than in the pure market equilibrium, but lower than in the socially efficient
17:630:34846:18:31:89:345:541:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:equilibrium (UG<UNG<USGandUI<UNI<USI).
17:631:34884:31:18:107:521:510:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 3 shows that NDAs improve over the pure market outcome as they
17:632:34958:18:18:89:520:492:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:help idea generators to capture a larger fraction of the value they generate. This
17:633:35040:18:18:89:526:474:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is reflected in the fact that∆N>∆, which shows that the net benefitofhaving
17:634:35115:18:18:89:521:456:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f7:B:an idea is higher when ideas are protected. For intermediate values ofψ(i.e.,ψ∈
17:635:35194:18:18:89:521:438:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f2:B:(ψO,ψN)) the equilibrium is more efficient than the market equilibrium, but still not
17:636:35279:18:18:89:520:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:socially optimal, as opportunistic incentives to to elaborate rather than generate ideas
17:637:35367:18:17:89:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:continue to exist. Only for sufficiently low values ofψ(i.e.,ψ<ψO)wefind that idea
17:638:35449:17:18:89:520:385:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generation always dominates the opportunist strategy. In this case, the equilibrium
17:639:35532:18:39:89:291:367:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is efficient, except for transaction costs.
17:640:35575:39:26:89:350:328:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:2.8  Are NDAs used in equilibrium?
17:641:35609:26:18:89:520:302:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The analysis of section 2.7 assumes that NDAs are signed by all agents. This section
17:642:35693:18:18:89:520:284:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:examines under what conditions NDAs will actually be used in equilibrium. Our goal
17:643:35775:18:18:89:520:266:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is to address a puzzle. Casual empirical observation suggests that NDAs are used
17:644:35855:18:18:89:520:248:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:very rarely by agents actively involved with new ideas. Even to the limited extent
17:645:35937:18:18:89:510:230:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:NDAs are employed, they are rarely used atthe initial stages of exchanging ideas.
17:646:36018:18:18:107:521:212:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Why are NDAs used so rarely by agents who share innovative ideas? Asking for
17:647:36094:18:18:89:521:194:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an NDA seems always beneficial for the issuer, the question is why the other party
17:648:36176:18:18:89:520:176:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:should sign it? Prior literature suggests that informational imperfections and the
17:649:36258:18:17:89:520:158:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:possibility of extortion limit the use of NDAs (see, in particular, Anton and Yao,
17:650:36340:17:18:89:521:141:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2002, 2004, 2005). We offer a parsimonious explanation for why agents may refuse to
17:651:36423:18:0:89:365:123:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:sign NDAs, namely that doing so may be suboptimal.
18:652:36475:0:18:107:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The NDA contracting game occurs when neither agent knows whether the other
18:653:36549:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:actually has an idea. We assume symmetric agents would sign an NDA only if the
18:654:36627:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:other also agrees to sign one - we return to this assumption at the end of the section.
18:655:36714:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Whether two agents choose to sign a mutual NDA depends on expectations about
18:656:36790:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:subsequent behavior.  To examine out-of-equilibrium beliefs of agents, we use the
18:657:36871:18:18:89:290:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:intuitive criterion of Cho-Kreps (1987).
18:658:36911:18:18:107:521:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The stage game proceeds as follows. Let agentApropose a mutual NDA, and
18:659:36982:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agentBeither accepts or reject. Agents then decide whether to disclose their ideas. If
18:660:37068:18:18:89:521:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:there is afit, the two negotiate the terms of cooperation, else they negotiate who will
18:661:37155:18:18:89:520:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:take the idea further. The behavior at the contracting stage is influenced by expec-
18:662:37239:18:18:89:520:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tations over whether or not disclosure occurs subsequent to a refusal to sign. There
18:663:37323:18:18:89:509:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:may be multiple equilibria supported by different beliefs about ex-post disclosure.
18:664:37406:18:18:107:521:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Wefirst establish the existence of an equilibrium where nobody signs NDAs. The
18:665:37484:18:18:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:key insight is that agents can never credibly commit to refuse disclosing their idea
18:666:37568:18:17:89:520:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:without a NDA. Intuitively, agents still want to disclose their ideas, even if their
18:667:37652:17:18:89:520:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:match refused to sign an NDA. This is a self-fulling equilibrium, because everyone
18:668:37734:18:18:89:275:420:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:expect same situation next period.14
18:669:37770:18:18:107:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Consider, starting from an equilibrium where no one uses NDAs, whether intro-
18:670:37847:18:18:89:521:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ducing NDAs constitutes a profitable deviation. The appendix shows that disclosure
18:671:37929:18:18:89:521:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:happens even without an NDA. Signing an NDA therefore does not affect the actual
18:672:38009:18:18:89:521:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exchange of ideas or value created. However, it affects the division of rents between
18:673:38094:18:18:89:520:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the two agents. This insight implies that using NDAs is a zero-sum game. In fact,
18:674:38175:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in the presence of transaction costs, using NDAs is a negative-sum game.15That is
18:675:38256:18:31:89:426:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:why introducing NDAs does not constitute a profitable deviation.
18:676:38320:31:18:89:416:263:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f19:C:Proposition 4(Existence of equilibrium without NDAs)
18:677:38372:18:18:89:520:245:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:There always exists an equilibrium in which agents never sign NDAs, and the equi-
18:678:38453:18:17:89:412:227:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:librium is the market equilibrium as described in Proposition 2.
18:679:38517:17:16:99:520:210:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:14The appendix shows that an agent cannot commit not to disclose even when he knows that
18:680:38605:16:12:89:520:194:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:the other agent is an opportunist.  The reason is that, in equilibrium, there are always enough
18:681:38700:12:12:89:520:182:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:opportunists (i.e.,θis sufficiently low), so that sharing an idea with a known opportunist in the
18:682:38797:12:12:89:520:170:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:current period is no worse than sharing an idea with an agent that is an opportunist with probability
18:683:38898:12:8:89:338:158:100:g_d0_f6:100:g_d0_f2:F:θin the next period. This result holds for all values ofδ.
18:684:38956:8:16:99:520:150:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:15Assuming a small transaction cost seems reasonable. However, the result continues to hold even
18:685:39052:16:12:89:524:134:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f8:F:forc=0, except that idea-bearers are now indifferent about signing NDAs. The model withc=0
18:686:39142:12:0:89:409:122:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:thus has knife-edge properties. Hence our focus on the model withc>0.
19:687:39213:0:18:107:524:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Tosketchtheproof,notethatifagentsdiscloseideaswithorwithoutNDAs,then
19:688:39281:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:NDAs either do nothing (when both or neither has an idea), or they transfer utility
19:689:39364:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:from one agent to another. Specifically, if both agents are idea-bearers, then NDAs
19:690:39447:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cancel out each other. Similarly, if both are opportunists, then NDAs are irrelevant.
19:691:39532:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:If, however, one agent is an idea-bearer and the other an opportunist, then an NDA
19:692:39614:18:18:89:521:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:has the effect of transferring utility from the opportunists to the idea-bearer. Having
19:693:39701:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:established that NDAs do not create value, consider now an equilibrium where nobody
19:694:39784:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:signs NDAs and examine whether a deviation whereAproposes using mutual NDAs
19:695:39859:18:18:89:521:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:breaks the equilibrium.Buses the intuitive criterion to make an inference aboutA’s
19:696:39941:18:18:89:526:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:type. ClearlyAcannot be an opportunist, since anOtype can never benefitfrom
19:697:40016:18:18:89:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an NDA.Bwould thus believe thatAis an idea-bearer. What isB’s best response?
19:698:40092:18:18:89:521:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:IfBis an opportunist, he would be worse offaccepting the NDA. However, even if
19:699:40170:18:18:89:521:491:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:Bis an idea-bearer, he would still refuse to sign the NDA, because the two NDAs
19:700:40249:18:18:89:521:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cancel out each other. So it is never worthwhile to incur the transactionscto write
19:701:40332:18:17:89:520:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:up NDAs that have no economic benefit. It follows that, starting from an equilibrium
19:702:40416:17:18:89:521:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:without NDAs, the deviation of offering NDA is always met with a negative response.
19:703:40499:18:18:89:521:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Moreover, the appendix shows thatAcannot commit not to disclose the idea even
19:704:40576:18:18:89:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:afterBrefuses the NDA. ThusA’s deviation to introduce an NDAs is not worthwhile.
19:705:40656:18:18:107:521:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 4 deals with a situation where no one uses NDAs, and shows that
19:706:40731:18:18:89:520:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this is a stable equilibrium. This still leaves open to possibility that there is another
19:707:40820:18:18:89:520:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium where NDAs are used. Intuitively, the equilibrium with NDAs is self-
19:708:40900:18:18:89:520:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:enforcing as long as agents refuse to disclose their ideas without an NDA. The key
19:709:40982:18:18:89:469:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:issue is thus whether refusing to disclose an idea without NDA is credible.
19:710:41057:18:18:107:521:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In the appendix we show that the refusal to disclose is not credible in many
19:711:41133:18:18:89:521:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:circumstances. Consider a deviation from the NDA equilibrium, where one agent,
19:712:41211:18:18:89:521:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:call himA, refuses to sign the NDA. We derive a condition of whenBwould still
19:713:41288:18:18:89:520:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:want to disclose his idea. Using the intuitive criterion, we show thatBwould not
19:714:41368:18:18:89:521:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:update his belief aboutAafter an NDA rejection, because both idea-bearers and
19:715:41445:18:18:89:521:204:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:opportunists prefer not to sign NDAs. WheneverB’s initial belief of having met an
19:716:41526:18:17:89:521:186:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea-bearer is sufficiently high (i.e.,θNis sufficiently high), he still prefers to discloses
19:717:41619:17:18:89:521:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the idea, even after an NDA rejection. This, however, makesA’s deviation of refusing
19:718:41703:18:18:89:520:151:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to sign the NDA profitable, implying that the equilibrium where all agents sign NDAs
19:719:41787:18:18:89:520:133:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:cannot be sustained. The key condition for an NDA equilibrium to be stable is thus
19:720:41869:18:0:89:520:115:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that the fraction of idea-bearers is not too high. Proposition 3 showed that for any
20:721:41955:0:18:89:521:707:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:ψ<ψO, the NDA equilibrium is efficient and has no opportunists, i.e.,θN=1.
20:722:42029:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We thus note that this equilibrium can never be sustained, because agents can never
20:723:42112:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:commit not to disclose their ideas. For the rangeψO<ψ<ψNwe haveθN<1.
20:724:42180:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The appendix derives a simple condition for when the refusal to disclose is credible
20:725:42264:18:31:89:366:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in this range. Formally we obtain the following result.
20:726:42319:31:18:89:397:604:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f19:C:Proposition 5(Existence of equilibrium with NDAs)
20:727:42368:18:19:89:520:586:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:The equilibrium where all agents sign NDAs described in Proposition 3 is not sus-
20:728:42449:19:0:89:202:567:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f7:C:tainable ifθN>3−
20:729:42465:0:16:208:214:575:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:C:2
20:730:42466:16:0:208:213:559:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f5:C:δ
20:731:42467:0:0:215:317:567:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:A:, or equivalently, if
20:732:42488:0:16:324:330:575:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:2
20:733:42489:16:0:324:330:559:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:3
20:734:42490:0:20:338:521:567:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f10:A:>δandψ<bψwherebψ=c+
20:735:42509:20:16:91:152:547:145:g_d0_f10:65:g_d0_f9:C:2−5δ+4δ2
20:736:42517:16:0:119:124:531:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f5:A:δ
20:737:42518:0:31:154:207:539:145:g_d0_f17:145:g_d0_f21:C:∆N>ψO.
20:738:42524:31:17:107:521:508:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 5 is an important and perhaps surprising result. It says that NDA
20:739:42601:17:18:89:520:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:contracts can arise endogenously only under limited circumstances. For a large range
20:740:42685:18:18:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of parameters, using NDA is simply not an equilibrium. This is in sharp contrast to
20:741:42768:18:18:89:504:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Proposition 4 which showed that the equilibrium without NDAs is always stable.
20:742:42846:18:19:107:521:437:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The condition for when NDAs can be used in equilibrium can be expressed in two
20:743:42924:19:0:89:251:418:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f7:B:ways. The conditionθN<3−
20:744:42948:0:17:256:262:426:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:A:2
20:745:42949:17:0:256:261:409:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f5:A:δ
20:746:42950:0:18:268:521:418:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:indicates that the rate of idea generation cannot
20:747:42999:18:18:89:520:400:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:be too high, or else there are too few opportunists in equilibrium to make the refusal
20:748:43085:18:18:89:521:382:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to disclose an idea credible. Put differently, when ideas are plentiful the expected
20:749:43169:18:18:89:520:364:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:payoffto share an unprotected idea is high, so agents do not bother to demand costly
20:750:43253:18:19:89:520:346:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:NDAs.  SinceθNis endogenous, we restate the condition exogenously in terms of
20:751:43330:19:0:89:229:327:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:ψ>bψ, which also requires
20:752:43355:0:16:235:241:335:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:C:2
20:753:43356:16:0:235:241:319:145:g_d0_f10:145:g_d0_f10:C:3
20:754:43357:0:18:246:521:327:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:A:<δ<1. So NDAs can be used only when there are
20:755:43402:18:18:89:521:309:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:fewer ideas in circulation and the cost of generating them is sufficiently high, so that
20:756:43490:18:18:89:405:291:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents become averse to disclose their ideas without an NDA.
20:757:43550:18:18:107:521:273:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The analysis so far is based on the adoption of a mutual NDA. Would anything
20:758:43626:18:18:89:521:255:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:change if we allow for unilateral NDAs? Mutual NDAs clearly require no transfer
20:759:43705:18:18:89:520:237:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:payments. In order to be willing to sign a unilateral NDA, it is conceivable that the
20:760:43790:18:18:89:520:219:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:NDA signee would require a payment from the NDA issuer. Such arrangements are
20:761:43867:18:18:89:520:201:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:hardly ever observed in practice.  Reassuringly, our model also predicts that such
20:762:43949:18:18:89:520:183:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:arrangements would never be used in equilibrium. The proof is in the appendix, we
20:763:44030:18:17:89:520:165:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:briefly sketch the main intuition. Proposition 4 continues to hold, because of the
20:764:44112:17:18:89:520:148:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:central insight that, starting from a equilibrium without NDAs, introducing NDAs is
20:765:44195:18:18:89:520:130:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a negative-sum game. While it is possible for one agent to design a unilateral NDA
20:766:44277:18:0:89:521:112:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:such that only idea-bearers would sign it, doing so is ultimately futile: the NDA
21:767:44360:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:doesn’t increase the joint utility, and offering ends up costing the issuer more than
21:768:44445:18:18:89:521:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:he can benefit from it. For Proposition 5, unilateral NDAs with side payments are
21:769:44526:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:unnecessary whenever the NDA equilibrium exists, nor do they affect the logic of how
21:770:44610:18:18:89:343:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a refusal to sign the NDA breaks the equilibrium.
21:771:44659:18:18:107:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our analysis identifies one important reason why agents involved in frequent idea
21:772:44740:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exchange do not sign NDAs: they become unnecessary when agents cannot commit
21:773:44816:18:18:89:521:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:not to disclose their ideas anyway, which occurs when ideas are sufficiently abun-
21:774:44898:18:18:89:124:581:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:dant.16
21:775:44905:18:18:107:521:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Next to contracts, agents can create a commitment to idea protection through
21:776:44981:18:18:89:520:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:reputation. The ability to create a reputation for not stealing ideas depends on the
21:777:45065:18:18:89:520:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:visibility of one’s action. We consider next the possibility that an agent invests in
21:778:45150:18:18:89:520:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:creating a visible environment among multiple agents.  In principle there may be
21:779:45230:18:18:89:520:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:multiple institutional arrangements that are supported by reputation mechanism.
21:780:45309:18:17:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Individuals may acquire a reputation, possible within some network structure, and
21:781:45390:17:18:89:524:456:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:organizationsmaybetherepositoriesofacollectivereputation.Wewillnotattempt
21:782:45463:18:18:89:520:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to provide a comprehensive characterization of all reputation mechanisms, but instead
21:783:45548:18:18:89:521:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:focus on one important reputation mechanism, namely thefirm (Kreps, 1986). This
21:784:45627:18:18:89:525:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:allowsustolinkouranalysistothelargereconomicdebateabouttherelativeroles
21:785:45698:18:45:89:374:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of markets versusfirms (Hart, 1995, Williamson, 1975).
21:786:45752:45:34:89:344:339:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:3  Idea circulation withfirms
21:787:45781:34:26:89:421:305:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3.1  Thefirm as a local reputation mechanism
21:788:45825:26:18:89:520:279:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The value of a reputation depends on the number of agents able to observe such
21:789:45903:18:18:89:520:261:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an opportunistic action, and whether they would choose to punish the deviation.
21:790:45982:18:18:89:521:243:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Clearly, a ‘global’ reputation could resolve idea stealing in our model, if it would imply
21:791:46072:18:18:89:520:225:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exclusion from any future idea exchange with anyone. Realistically, most actions are
21:792:46156:18:18:89:520:207:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:visible only among a few agents directly or indirectly involved. Firms may be seen as
21:793:46241:18:18:89:520:189:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:governance mechanisms to overcome individual opportunism. We propose to think of
21:794:46321:18:18:89:521:171:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms as having ‘local’ transparency among afinite set of agents that we call employees,
21:795:46409:18:17:89:472:153:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:reflecting a natural information distinction between insiders and outsiders.
21:796:46485:17:16:99:520:136:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:16Obviously there may be other reasons not modelled here for why NDAs are not used, such as
21:797:46576:16:0:89:518:120:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:the risk that an NDA could be used to extort rents even if no true violation of the NDA occurred.
22:798:46675:0:18:107:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Firms make use of a different legal arrangement than NDAs to protect against idea
22:799:46756:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:stealing, namely trade secret law. Whereas NDAs pertain to transactions among unre-
22:800:46839:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:lated parties, and are relatively rarely used in practice, trade secret law automatically
22:801:46928:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:bind parties related through employment contracts. Agents accepting employment
22:802:47006:18:18:89:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:commit not to take ideas out of thefirms, so that thefirm defines a legal boundary
22:803:47088:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for the circulation of internal ideas. As a result, once the idea is recorded as afirm
22:804:47174:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:initiative, employees can exchange their ideas without the risk of theft. Naturally,
22:805:47258:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:this requires that thefirm monitors its boundaries, which may be costly (Liebeskind,
22:806:47342:18:18:89:185:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:1997, Chou, 2007).
22:807:47360:18:18:107:521:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We model thefirm as an enabler of idea circulation among afinite set of agents.
22:808:47439:18:18:89:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Thefirm claims ownership on all internally generated ideas. Since employees’ ideas are
22:809:47525:18:18:89:520:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:unobservable until reported, thefirm needs to provide appropriate incentives for idea
22:810:47610:18:18:89:520:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:disclosure, and to protect them within its own boundaries, pursuing any idea theft.
22:811:47693:18:18:89:521:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Therewardiscredibleonlyifthefirm owner would lose more from taking advantage
22:812:47769:18:17:89:520:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:by using ideas without adequately compensating their generators. Visibility enables
22:813:47852:17:18:89:520:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to develop a local reputation, where insiders trust the reputed agent until proven
22:814:47934:18:18:89:521:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:wrong(Kreps,1986).Thusareputationmaybeupheldinaninfinite game of perfect
22:815:48006:18:18:89:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:certainty as long as thefirm adequately rewards its employees, else they all leave and
22:816:48092:18:18:89:207:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:thefirm loses all value.
22:817:48116:18:18:107:521:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Naturally, creating a reputation is costly. We assume that afirm owner needs
22:818:48192:18:18:89:520:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to make a large sunk investment to establish a process by which her actions are
22:819:48271:18:18:89:520:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:visible to afinite set of agents. To define this choice, we assume free entry and an
22:820:48355:18:18:89:521:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:upward-sloping supply curve offirms. Specifically, thejthentrant faces a sunkfixed
22:821:48437:18:18:89:521:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:costKj,whereKjis distributed according to a cumulative distributionΩ(Kj)with
22:822:48513:18:18:89:520:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:densityω(Kj)over the rangeKj∈[Kmin,Kmax].Kjhere reflects the sunk expense
22:823:48586:18:18:89:521:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to establish afirm, which includes the cost of creating visibility, plus otherfixed costs
22:824:48675:18:17:89:316:240:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:that are increasing in the number offirms.17
22:825:48719:17:18:107:521:223:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:We assume that transparency of actions can only be achieved with afinite set of
22:826:48798:18:18:89:521:205:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents, the size of which we denote byE. Formally, the investmentKjallows the
22:827:48875:18:18:89:521:187:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firm owner to establish a reputation amongEagents. Thefirm owner hires these
22:828:48951:18:18:89:521:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:agents as employees. We assume thatEis large butfinite, and for tractability treat
22:829:49033:18:18:89:520:151:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:it as exogenous.18Once an owner commits to managing afirm, she no longer can
22:830:49109:18:12:99:456:133:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:?:17This assumption reflects some scarce resource, such as increasing location costs.
22:831:49192:12:0:99:520:121:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:18In principle we could allow for the possibility that larger investments create transparency among
23:832:49293:0:18:89:244:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generate or complement ideas.
23:833:49322:18:18:107:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Suppose thefirm’s reputation depends on maintaining a promise to reward idea
23:834:49398:18:18:89:526:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generators with an amountbzforeachideaoriginatedandimplementedinternally.
23:835:49471:18:18:89:521:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The reputation condition ensures thatfirm owners prefer to maintain their reputation
23:836:49555:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:over a deviation where the owner lets employees implement their ideas but refuses to
23:837:49639:18:18:89:521:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:pay any bonus. The maximal deviation payoffwould occur in the rare event when
23:838:49716:18:18:89:521:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:allEhad completed ideas at the same time. Not paying them would give the owner
23:839:49794:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a deviation value ofEbz. After that the owner earns the normal agent return ofUO.
23:840:49875:18:33:89:295:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:So the reputation condition is as follows
23:841:49916:33:32:265:345:530:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f17:C:Ebz+UO<δΠ
23:842:49925:32:18:107:521:498:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Later we derive the equilibrium value of thefirm and formally prove this condition
23:843:50007:18:18:89:521:480:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is always satisfied forδsufficiently close to1. This is a standard result, since the
23:844:50091:18:18:89:521:462:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:benefits of losing a reputation on the left hand side are bounded, whereas the benefits
23:845:50178:18:18:89:521:444:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of keeping a reputation on the right had side is increasing inδ. For the remainder of
23:846:50263:18:39:89:367:426:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:theanalysisweassumethatthisconditionissatisfied.
23:847:50311:39:26:89:327:387:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:C:3.2  Idea circulation withinfirms
23:848:50344:26:18:89:520:361:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:To establish a claim on an idea, upon its disclosure by its inventor it is “recorded”
23:849:50429:18:18:89:521:343:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as an internal project, in a verifiable form. Thus “bureaucratic procedures” and a
23:850:50511:18:18:89:520:325:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:“paper trail” are essential for the internal reward system, and for internal ideas to be
23:851:50599:18:17:89:521:307:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:covered by trade secret laws. We assume thatfirms can always prevent idea stealing
23:852:50681:17:18:89:520:290:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:by threatening legal action.  Once an idea is reported, the generator is assigned
23:853:50762:18:18:89:520:272:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the task to implement it via internal matching. In managerial terms, he becomes
23:854:50841:18:18:89:520:254:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an “internal project champion” or an “intrapreneur.” Since no employee can leak
23:855:50920:18:18:89:521:236:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the idea outside thefirm, the generator can count on cooperation from all internal
23:856:51002:18:18:89:521:218:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:listeners. Thefirm uses an internal rotation system that corresponds to the random
23:857:51084:18:18:89:521:200:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:matching in markets. For simplicity we assume that thefirm can avoid matching
23:858:51161:18:18:89:521:182:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:repeatedly two agents who didn’tfind afitontheirfirst match. Employees may leave
23:859:51241:18:21:89:521:164:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:thefirm at will, but they need permission from thefirm to pursue any reported idea.
23:860:51324:21:12:89:521:143:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:a larger set of agent, so thatEwould be an increasing function ofKj. This would endogenize size
23:861:51419:12:12:89:521:131:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:offirm boundaries. In an earlier version, Hellmann and Perotti (2005) we allow for this, but note
23:862:51516:12:0:89:400:119:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:that this extension adds complexity without offering additional insight.
24:863:51590:0:18:107:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:To make the analysis of thefirm tractable and comparable to the market outcome,

24:866:51827:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The major difference is that afirm will fail to complete all ideas internally.  The
24:867:51910:18:18:89:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:next subsection shows that if there is no internalfit, then it is optimal to allow idea
24:868:51997:18:18:89:349:617:145:g_d0_f2:65:g_d0_f2:B:generators to pursue their ideas outside thefirm.19

24:871:52213:18:18:89:473:563:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms. For largeE, any deviations from the steady state become negligible.
24:872:52287:18:18:107:521:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:LetFbe the number of agents that an idea-bearer talks to within afirm. This

28:1072:60742:48:18:107:521:337:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Clearly, the utility of independent agents increases with the number offirms. More
28:1073:60824:18:18:89:521:319:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms means that more ideas leak out into the market, increasing the likelihood that
28:1074:60908:18:18:89:414:301:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:an opportunist encounters an idea to either implement or steal.
28:1075:60971:18:18:107:521:283:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The comparative statics ofUOare quite different from the corollary to Proposition
28:1076:61052:18:18:89:520:265:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2,sincenowthemarketpayoffis no longer determined by the indifference condition

29:1084:61547:0:18:89:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:We call this thefirm equation (F), it expresses thefirm densitynFas a function
29:1085:61625:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of market utilityUO, also depicted in Figure 1.  Fundamentally, theFcurve is a

29:1088:61830:48:18:107:520:605:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f2:A:Firm equilibrium:TheFcurve is downwards sloping, i.e.,nFis decreasing in

29:1090:61955:48:18:107:521:539:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The main insight is that a higher utility for market agents increases thefirm’s
29:1091:62034:18:18:89:521:521:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:employment costs and thus reduces the density offirms.22The number offirms is

29:1094:62195:18:17:107:520:467:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Since theMis upward sloping and theFcurve downward sloping, there exists
29:1095:62267:17:18:89:520:450:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a unique equilibrium. We are now in a position to fully characterize the equilibrium
29:1096:62351:18:31:89:230:432:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and its comparative statics.
29:1097:62379:31:18:89:521:401:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f21:F:Proposition 8(i) Forψ∈[ψM,ψF)there exists an equilibrium such that all ideas
29:1098:62455:18:0:89:309:383:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f5:C:are generated insidefirms, but a fractionφ
29:1099:62497:0:7:309:314:390:65:g_d0_f11:65:g_d0_f11:?:F

29:1101:62527:18:18:89:521:365:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:(ii) The equilibrium is determined by the intersection of theMandFcurves. The
29:1102:62604:18:18:89:259:347:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:comparative statics are as follows

29:1105:62746:31:18:107:521:280:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Forψ∈[ψM,ψF)firms enter and hire employees to generate ideas, while market

29:1108:62980:18:17:89:520:226:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2 shows that higher generation costsψalways decrease the number offirms, as well
29:1109:63060:17:18:89:520:209:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as the utility of market agents. This can be seen from the fact that only theFcurve
29:1110:63143:18:18:89:162:191:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:depends onψ.
29:1111:63155:18:18:107:521:173:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 3 shows the effect of increasing the value of ideasz. The utility of mar-
