29:1113:63309:18:16:99:521:137:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:22Note that while it is individually rational for afirm to allow uncompleted ideas to leave, in the
29:1114:63408:16:12:89:520:121:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:aggregate this increases the reward to opportunism in the market, and thus thefirm cost to reward
29:1115:63505:12:0:89:205:109:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:internal ideas for allfirms.
30:1116:63535:0:18:89:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Intuitively, a higher value of ideas should increasefirm profits and thus increase the
30:1117:63621:18:18:89:521:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:density offirmsnF,asreflectedintheoutwardshiftoftheFcurve. However, a
30:1118:63690:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:higher value of ideas also increases the utility of market agents, and thus the cost
30:1119:63774:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of hiring employees, as represented by the upward shift of theMcurve. The net
30:1120:63851:18:18:89:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of these two effects is ambiguous. In the appendix we show how for sufficiently low
30:1121:63934:18:18:89:521:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:values ofnF(when the distributionΩputs sufficient weight on higher values ofK)
30:1122:64012:18:39:89:253:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the net effect is always positive.
30:1123:64046:39:25:89:517:560:209:g_d0_f1:209:g_d0_f1:F:3.5  Coexistence when bothfirm and market generate ideas
30:1124:64102:25:18:89:521:535:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Whenψ<ψM, idea generation in markets is feasible. Is there still an opportunity for
30:1125:64185:18:18:89:521:517:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms to organize a parallel process of generating and circulating ideas? The answer
30:1126:64269:18:18:89:520:499:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is yes, because the market still allows for idea stealing, thus implicitly rewarding op-
30:1127:64357:18:18:89:520:481:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:portunism. Firms can ensure a safer return to idea generation, and thus increase idea
30:1128:64442:18:18:89:521:463:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generation overall. However, ideas leavingfirms increase the return to opportunism,
30:1129:64525:18:18:89:395:445:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:which reduces the rate of idea generation by market agents.
30:1130:64584:18:18:107:521:427:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The new equilibrium is similar to the one discussed in section 3.4., except that
30:1131:64664:18:18:89:525:409:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ideas are now generated both infirms and markets. TheFcurveisthesameasin
30:1132:64736:18:18:89:521:391:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:section 3.4, but theMequation is different. In fact, the results from Propositions 2
30:1133:64820:18:47:89:461:373:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and its corollary apply once again, which affects theMcurve as follows:
30:1134:64891:47:18:107:521:326:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f2:A:Market equilibrium (part 2):Forψ<ψM,theMcurve is entirelyflat, i.e.,
30:1135:64959:18:47:89:439:308:145:g_d0_f5:145:g_d0_f2:B:UOis independent ofnF.UOis increasing inz, and decreasing inψ.
30:1136:65021:47:18:107:526:261:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Forψ<ψM,theMcurve no longer depends on the density offirmsnF.Thekey
30:1137:65088:18:18:89:520:243:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:intuition is that once ideas are generated in the market, the utility of market agents
30:1138:65174:18:18:89:521:225:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:no longer depends onfirms, but regains its own dynamics, as described in Proposition
30:1139:65258:18:18:89:520:207:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:2 and its corollary. We are now in a position to characterize the equilibrium and its
30:1140:65343:18:29:89:191:189:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:comparative statics.
30:1141:65363:29:18:89:521:160:145:g_d0_f1:145:g_d0_f21:F:Proposition 9(i) Forψ<ψMthere exists an equilibrium such that ideas are gen-
30:1142:65439:18:18:89:520:142:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:erated both insidefirms and in the market.  The equilibrium is determined by the
30:1143:65519:18:18:89:521:124:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:F:intersection of theflatMand the downwards slopingFcurves. The comparative
30:1144:65592:18:0:89:195:106:145:g_d0_f21:145:g_d0_f21:C:statics are as follows
31:1145:65616:0:18:89:347:707:145:g_d0_f7:145:g_d0_f21:C:◦An increase inψdecreasesUObut increasesnF.
31:1146:65659:18:49:89:298:689:145:g_d0_f7:145:g_d0_f21:C:◦An increase inzincreasesUOandnF.
31:1147:65692:49:18:107:521:640:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Proposition 9 differs from Proposition 8, because in Proposition 9 market idea
31:1148:65770:18:18:89:521:622:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generation directly competes with idea generation insidefirms. The reason thatfirms
31:1149:65853:18:18:89:520:604:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:continue to exist, even when markets generate ideas, is thatfirms can solve some of
31:1150:65936:18:18:89:520:586:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the inefficiencies that occur in the market. Specifically,firms can provide incentives
31:1151:66022:18:18:89:520:568:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to their employees that discourage idea stealing and opportunism. This ensures that
31:1152:66105:18:18:89:521:550:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:withinfirms all employees only generate and circulate their own ideas. However,firms
31:1153:66189:18:18:89:520:532:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:can only provide a limited number of employee interactions, so that some employees
31:1154:66271:18:18:89:520:514:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:leave with their ideas. In equilibrium, the strengths of market interactions, offering
31:1155:66357:18:18:89:459:496:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:unlimited matching opportunities, thus augments the strengths offirms.
31:1156:66427:18:17:107:521:478:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:ThemostsurprisingpartofProposition9isthatthefirm densitynFis actually
31:1157:66496:17:18:89:521:461:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:increasing inψ. The intuition is that higher generation costs discourage idea creation
31:1158:66582:18:18:89:521:443:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:in bothfirms and markets, but that markets are more affected because of the stealing
31:1159:66666:18:18:89:134:425:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:problem.
31:1160:66674:18:18:107:521:407:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 4 integrates insights from Proposition 8 and 9, showing how the number
31:1161:66751:18:18:89:521:389:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:offirms (nF) depends on idea generation costs (ψ) across the entire parameter range.
31:1162:66835:18:18:89:520:371:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:For low values ofψ,thenumberoffirmsisincreasinginψ, as shown in Proposition
31:1163:66910:18:18:89:527:353:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:9. Figure 4 shows that idea generation in the market declines rapidly withψ.This
31:1164:66990:18:18:89:521:335:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:means that the relative importancefirms actually increases, allowing for the density
31:1165:67074:18:18:89:520:317:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:offirmsnFto actually increase inψ.BeyondψMidea generation ceases up in the
31:1166:67148:18:18:89:521:299:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:market entirely, so that ideas are only generated insidefirms. At this stage, higher
31:1167:67232:18:18:89:528:281:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:generation costs discouragefirm activity, so thatnFdecreases withψ.Firmscease
31:1168:67309:18:45:89:190:263:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to exist beyondψF.
31:1169:67327:45:30:89:409:218:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:4  Extensions and empirical evidence
31:1170:67363:30:18:89:521:188:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Our approach has yielded two main results.  Thefirst concerns the effect of idea
31:1171:67443:18:18:89:520:170:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:density on the open exchange of ideas. The second suggests an important symbiotic
31:1172:67524:18:17:89:521:152:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:relationship between openfirms and markets, withfirms incubating ideas and markets
31:1173:67606:17:18:89:521:135:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:both creating their own ideas as well as refining those that could not be elaborated
31:1174:67690:18:0:89:154:117:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:withinfirms.
32:1175:67704:0:18:107:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:A natural environment to discuss the coincidence of these effects is Silicon Valley,
32:1176:67788:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:often taken as evidence that innovation thrives in a free market environment. Hamel
32:1177:67871:18:18:89:520:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:(1999) writes that "in Silicon Valley, ideas, capital, and talent circulate freely, gather-
32:1178:67962:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ing into whatever combinations are most likely to generate innovation ... traditional
32:1179:68047:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:companies... spend their energy in resource allocation... the Valley operates through
32:1180:68132:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:resource attraction—a system that nurtures innovation. . . . talent is free to go to the
32:1181:68220:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:companies offering the most exhilarating work and the greatest potential rewards".
32:1182:68302:18:18:89:520:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:This is broadly consistent with our sketch of ideas as combination of expertise, cir-
32:1183:68387:18:18:89:520:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:culating to seek the right match without using NDA contracts, whilefirms reward
32:1184:68466:18:18:89:520:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:creative agents and agents with unresolved ideas moving out offirms to start up
32:1185:68545:18:18:89:135:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ventures.
32:1186:68554:18:18:107:521:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The intense and open idea exchange in Silicon Valley may seem puzzling, since
32:1187:68631:18:18:89:520:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:California actually has a fairly weak tradition of protecting intellectual property, so
32:1188:68718:18:18:89:520:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:that is not clear how idea generation may be rewarded (see Gilson 1999, Hyde, 1998).
32:1189:68802:18:17:89:521:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Our model offers a clue, showing that entrepreneurialfirm formation and large multi-
32:1190:68886:17:18:89:520:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:productfirms are symbiotic. Largefirms are a natural source of innovative ideas,
32:1191:68966:18:18:89:520:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:which at times may be realized only if matched with talented market agents.  In
32:1192:69045:18:18:89:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:turn, a market will attract creative entrepreneurial individuals and support a free
32:1193:69128:18:18:89:521:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:circulation of ideas only for a certain idea density. In our context, a high density of
32:1194:69215:18:18:89:521:366:145:g_d0_f3:145:g_d0_f2:B:firms increases idea density in surrounding markets. The open environment in Silicon
32:1195:69299:18:18:89:521:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Valley may thus thrive thanks to the historical presence of largefirms in the area
32:1196:69381:18:18:89:520:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:acting as idea incubators, in addition to the incubating role played by top academic
32:1197:69465:18:18:89:150:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:institutions.
32:1198:69478:18:18:107:521:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Indeed, there are many largefirms in the area, which according to Business Week
32:1199:69557:18:18:89:521:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:accounted for a remarkable 20% of thelargesthigh techfirms in the world in 1997.
32:1200:69637:18:18:89:521:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Gompers, Lerner and Scharfstein (2005) provide extensive evidence on the role that
32:1201:69719:18:18:89:520:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:large corporations play in entrepreneurial spawning. Consistent with our mobility

32:1204:69955:18:17:89:520:186:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for innovative ideas which later are developed in new ventures by departing employ-
32:1205:70038:17:19:89:526:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ees.23Aoki (2001) and Saxenian (1994) argue thatfirmswithporousboundaries
32:1206:70111:19:15:99:521:150:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:23Most R&D is still performed in establishedfirms. The National Science Foundation estimates
32:1207:70203:15:12:89:520:135:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:private industrial R&D spending at $180 billion in 2003 (latest available data).  In comparison,

33:1210:70433:0:18:89:521:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:increases the mutual localflow of ideas, while a secretive corporate culture - such
33:1211:70516:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:as the hierarchical approach to R&D in Japan and Europe, as well as in some large

33:1215:70834:18:18:107:521:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Naturally, many employee-generated ideas are implemented internally. Companies
33:1216:70912:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:such as Google or 3M pride themselves of continually generating new ideas in house

33:1231:72019:18:18:107:521:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:In addition to idea incubation insidefirms, our model shows idea generation can
33:1232:72098:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:also occur by independent agents, even if exposed to free-riding and idea stealing
33:1233:72180:18:18:89:520:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:incentives. Many entrepreneurs generated their ideas on their own and found appro-

33:1237:72506:18:18:89:521:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:whereasfirms focus on larger scale, complex ideas with substantial ex-ante invest-

33:1241:72822:18:18:107:521:151:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:One of the sources for relatively low-cost production of ideas are universities. In

34:1254:73849:18:18:107:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:To offer a fair comparison offirms and markets, we assume that their probability
34:1255:73929:18:18:89:521:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of meeting a complementor (φ)isthesame.Inreality,firmsdospecializeindifferent
34:1256:74006:18:18:89:521:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:types of ideas, seeking employees with complementary skills. Yetfirms cannot plan

34:1264:74644:18:18:107:521:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:A common perception, shaped by success stories, is that returns are greater for
34:1265:74723:18:18:89:520:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:entrepreneurs than intrapreneurs or employees. The empirical evidence in contrast in-
34:1266:74808:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:dicates that the average risk-adjusted return to entrepreneurship is quite low (Hamil-

34:1270:75151:18:18:89:520:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:they have more chances of circulating their idea in a protected environment. Entre-
34:1271:75234:18:18:89:520:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:preneurs by contrast receive the full value of their ideas, but have to share it with
34:1272:75319:18:17:89:521:204:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:among founders. The model predicts that if there is afit within the team, complemen-
34:1273:75403:17:18:89:520:187:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:tors receive as a substantial portion of founder equity, even if they didn’t contribute
34:1274:75490:18:19:89:521:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the idea. Consistent with this, Marx and Wasserman (2008)find that equal splits
34:1275:75569:19:15:99:521:150:49:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:24Employees may also leavefirms without disclosing ideas if these are exceptionally valuable
34:1276:75661:15:12:89:520:135:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:(Chatterjee and Rossi-Hansberg, 2008), iffirms do not adjust reward (see Gambardella and Panico,
34:1277:75757:12:0:89:457:123:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2006), or iffirms are pursuing a strategy of discouraging spin-offs (Hellmann, 2006).
35:1278:75844:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:among founders are common, even if only one of the founders contributed the initial
35:1279:75927:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:idea. Evidence on idea stealing is naturally harder to come by. One well-known story
35:1280:76011:18:18:89:509:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:is Steve Job’s taking the idea of a computer mouse during his visit of Xerox Parc.
35:1281:76093:18:18:107:521:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our model provides a joint explanation for a variety of different types of new
35:1282:76171:18:18:89:521:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:ventures: internal ventures, spin-offs and start-ups. As limitations, the model does
35:1283:76255:18:18:89:520:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:not allow any form of idea stealing withinfirms, and assume that the reputation
35:1284:76334:18:18:89:520:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:condition holds at all times. In an earlier version (Hellmann Perotti 2005) we showed
35:1285:76419:18:18:89:521:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:how these extreme assumptions could be relaxed. For instance, thefirm might be
35:1286:76497:18:18:89:520:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:willing to compensate employees for smaller ideas, but may have an incentive to
35:1287:76576:18:18:89:492:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:renege on highly valuable ideas (as in the classic corporate story at TetraPak).
35:1288:76656:18:18:107:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Our model emphasizes the role offirm boundaries on idea circulation. In a related
35:1289:76737:18:18:89:521:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:vein, Azoulay (2004)finds that pharmaceuticalfirms, while very active in outsourcing,
35:1290:76822:18:18:89:521:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:maintain strongfirm boundaries around knowledge intensive projects. Kremp and
35:1291:76899:18:18:89:521:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Mairesse (2004) alsofind a positive relationship betweenfirms’ internal knowledge
35:1292:76980:18:17:89:374:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:management systems and their innovative performance.
35:1293:77032:17:18:107:521:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, one may ask if venture capital operate in some alternative form. As they
35:1294:77113:18:18:89:520:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:clearly seek to build a reputation for fair dealing among local contacts, in this sense
35:1295:77200:18:18:89:521:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:their behavior may resemble that offirms in our model.  However, there are also
35:1296:77279:18:18:89:521:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:fundamental differences. First, we study ideas at the very initial formation stage,
35:1297:77362:18:18:89:521:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:when the product is not yet defined and there can be no business plan, well before
35:1298:77444:18:18:89:520:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the issue offinancing arises. Even so-called ‘seed stage’ venture capitalists do not
35:1299:77528:18:18:89:521:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:typically get involved at such a stage when neither the product nor the founding team
35:1300:77613:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:are in place. Second, the governance of venture capitalfirms has a looser, network-
35:1301:77696:18:18:89:521:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:style structure, rather than the hierarchical structure offirms. They also seeks ideas
35:1302:77782:18:18:89:520:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exclusively outside, in the language of the model acting as late stage complementors.
35:1303:77867:18:18:89:521:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:In any case, as mentioned before, we concur thatfirms are not the only solution to
35:1304:77949:18:18:89:520:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:control idea stealing. Further exploring alternative governance mechanisms of the
35:1305:78030:18:45:89:346:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:protection of ideas is a promising area of research.
35:1306:78082:45:29:89:238:177:301:g_d0_f1:301:g_d0_f1:C:5Conclusions
35:1307:78094:29:18:89:520:148:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Early stage novel ideas may be seen as incomplete concepts needing to be matched
35:1308:78174:18:18:89:520:130:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with some complementary expertise for completion, yet facing uncertainty as to what
35:1309:78257:18:0:89:521:112:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:exactly the required match may be. We analyze the trade-offbetween the necessity
36:1310:78339:0:18:89:520:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to share widely ideas, to identify agents able to elaborate them further, and the risk
36:1311:78425:18:18:89:520:689:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of idea stealing associated with sharing nonexcludable information. A free circulation
36:1312:78511:18:18:89:521:671:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:of ideas in a market setting is efficient for elaboration, but fails to fully reward effort
36:1313:78602:18:18:89:520:653:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:for invention. We show that individuals may voluntarily joinfirms with reputational
36:1314:78685:18:18:89:520:635:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:capital to ensure that their ideas receive feedback without being stolen. Firms create
36:1315:78771:18:18:89:521:617:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:alegalfirm boundary which may contain appropriation of others’ ideas, and manage
36:1316:78851:18:18:89:521:599:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a controlled circulation of ideas along with a credible reward system. Yetfirms have
36:1317:78935:18:18:89:520:581:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:limited capacity to elaborate ideas internally, and may therefore allow agents to leave
36:1318:79022:18:18:89:520:563:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to try out developing incomplete ideas in new ventures. Our model thus describes
36:1319:79102:18:18:89:521:545:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:a natural symbiosis between the ability offirms to sustain idea generation and the
36:1320:79184:18:18:89:521:527:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:comparative advantage of market in elaborating ideas. This approach rationalizes the
36:1321:79268:18:18:89:520:509:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:process of idea incubation and spawning which seems to describe well the open ex-
36:1322:79349:18:18:89:520:491:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:change of ideas acrossfirms and markets typical of successful innovative environments
36:1323:79434:18:18:89:201:473:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:such as Silicon Valley.
36:1324:79457:18:17:107:524:455:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:The approach suggests interesting directions for future research. Afirstissueisto
36:1325:79538:17:18:89:520:438:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:understand what environments are most conducive to promote both idea generation
36:1326:79617:18:18:89:520:420:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and completion, and to explain the movement of ideas by the incentives of inventors
36:1327:79700:18:18:89:356:402:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to seek the appropriate environment for completion.
36:1328:79751:18:18:107:521:384:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:A compelling new research agenda focuses on the generation of ideas in academia
36:1329:79830:18:18:89:520:366:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:and industry (Aghion, Dewatripont and Stein, 2009).  Academic researchers aim
36:1330:79907:18:18:89:521:348:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:at diffusing their ideas, so they rarely capture any value created by their discoveries.
36:1331:79995:18:18:89:520:330:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:The academic publication system may ensure a basis for public reward, which sustains
36:1332:80079:18:18:89:520:312:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:the freedom of investigation and idea circulation which researchers value. Our model
36:1333:80163:18:18:89:520:294:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:suggests that the innovative ideas incubated in academia may have a disproportional
36:1334:80246:18:18:89:520:276:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:effect in supporting an open exchange environment where ideas circulate easily and
36:1335:80328:18:18:89:520:258:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:widely. The empirical results in Aghion et al. (2009) support the importance of a
36:1336:80409:18:18:89:520:240:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:free circulation of ideas, to ensure the maximum degree of elaboration and ultimately
36:1337:80494:18:18:89:145:222:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:innovation.
36:1338:80505:18:18:107:521:204:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:A:Another issue is the self-selection of agents operating infirms and markets. Agents
36:1339:80588:18:17:89:521:186:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:with a greater predisposition to complement ideas may be better offoutsidefirms,
36:1340:80668:17:18:89:520:169:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:where they can expect better rewards. Examples are serial entrepreneurs, venture
36:1341:80748:18:18:89:520:151:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:capitalists, seasoned angel investors, and professional mentors and consultants able
36:1342:80832:18:18:89:520:133:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:to help entrepreneurs to turn their ideas into viable businesses (Lee et al., 2000).
36:1343:80916:18:0:89:520:115:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:Such specialized agents may organize alternative organizational structures, such as
37:1344:81001:0:46:89:512:707:145:g_d0_f2:145:g_d0_f2:B:partnership and networks, to obtain greater rewards thanfirms would grant them.
